Widget-->\n</div> <!--box outer-->\n</div> <!--End Inner-->\n<div class=\"inner\">\n<div class=\"container\">\n<div class=\"main\">\n<div class=\"box_outer\">\n<article class=\"cat_article\">\n<h1 class=\"cat_article_title\">Analog Input using Arduino</h1>\n<div class=\"article_meta\">\n<span class=\"meta_date\">Posted date:  <strong>May 17, 2014</strong></span>\n<span class=\"meta_cat\">In:  <strong><a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/projects/\" rel=\"category tag\">Projects</a>, <a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/projects/pwm-projects/\" rel=\"category tag\">PWM Projects</a></strong></span>\n<span class=\"meta_sap\">|</span> \n<span class=\"meta_tags\">  Tags: <a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/tag/analog/\" rel=\"tag\">analog</a>, <a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/tag/arduino/\" rel=\"tag\">arduino</a>, <a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/tag/input/\" rel=\"tag\">input</a><br> </span>\n</div> <!--article meta-->\n<div id=\"article_content\" class=\"single_article_content\">\n<p><!-- Quick Adsense WordPress Plugin: http://quicksense.net/ --></p>\n<div style=\"float:none;margin:0px;\">\n<div style=\"float:left;margin:-30px 10px 10px 0;\"><script async=\"\" src=\"//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js\"></script><br>\n<!-- Arduino All-Internal-Pages ATF Top 336by280 --><br>\n<ins class=\"adsbygoogle\" style=\"display:inline-block;width:336px;height:280px\" data-ad-client=\"ca-pub-8393123498169788\" data-ad-slot=\"3287473095\" data-adsbygoogle-status=\"done\"><ins id=\"aswift_1_expand\" style=\"display:inline-table;border:none;height:280px;margin:0;padding:0;position:relative;visibility:visible;width:336px;background-color:transparent\"><ins i=this.id,s=window.google_iframe_oncopy,H=s&amp;&amp;s.handlers,h=H&amp;&amp;H[i],w=this.contentWindow,d;try{d=w.document}catch(e){}if(h&amp;&amp;d&amp;&amp;(!d.body||!d.body.firstChild)){if(h.call){setTimeout(h,0)}else if(h.match){try{h=s.upd(h,i)}catch(e){}w.location.replace(h)}}\" id=\"aswift_1\" name=\"aswift_1\" style=\"left:0;position:absolute;top:0;\"></iframe></ins></ins></ins><br>\n<script>\n(adsbygoogle = window.adsbygoogle || []).push({});\n</script>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>A potentiometer is a simple knob that provides a variable resistance, which you can read into the Arduino board as an analog value. In this example, you’ll connect a poterntiometer to one of the Arduino’s analog inputs to control the rate at which the built-in LED on pin 13 blinks.</p>\n<h3>Circuit</h3>\n<p><a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-4039\" alt=\"Arduino Analog Input\" src=\"http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input.jpg\" width=\"594\" height=\"537\" srcset=\"http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input.jpg 594w, http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input-300x271.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 594px) 100vw, 594px\"></a></p>\n<p><!-- Quick Adsense WordPress Plugin: http://quicksense.net/ --></p>\n<div style=\"float:none;margin:10px 0 10px 0;text-align:center;\">\n<script async=\"\" src=\"//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js\"></script><br>\n<!-- link_ad_responsive --><br>\n<ins class=\"adsbygoogle\" style=\"display: block; height: 30px;\" data-ad-client=\"ca-pub-8393123498169788\" data-ad-slot=\"1687436295\" data-ad-format=\"link\" data-adsbygoogle-status=\"done\"><ins id=\"aswift_2_expand\" style=\"display:inline-table;border:none;height:30px;margin:0;padding:0;position:relative;visibility:visible;width:609px;background-color:transparent\"><ins id=\"aswift_2_anchor\" style=\"display:block;border:none;height:30px;margin:0;padding:0;position:relative;visibility:visible;width:609px;background-color:transparent\"><iframe width=\"609\" height=\"30\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" vspace=\"0\" hspace=\"0\" allowtransparency=\"true\" scrolling=\"no\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" onload=\"var i=this.id,s=window.google_iframe_oncopy,H=s&amp;&amp;s.handlers,h=H&amp;&amp;H[i],w=this.contentWindow,d;try{d=w.document}catch(e){}if(h&amp;&amp;d&amp;&amp;(!d.body||!d.body.firstChild)){if(h.call){setTimeout(h,0)}else if(h.match){try{h=s.upd(h,i)}catch(e){}w.location.replace(h)}}\" id=\"aswift_2\" name=\"aswift_2\" style=\"left:0;position:absolute;top:0;\"></iframe></ins></ins></ins><br>\n<script>\n(adsbygoogle = window.adsbygoogle || []).push({});\n</script>\n</div>\n<p>image developed using&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.fritzing.org/\" rel=\"nofollow external nofollow\" onclick=\"this.target='_blank';\" target=\"_blank\">Fritzing</a>. For more circuit examples, see the&nbsp;<a href=\"http://fritzing.org/projects/\" rel=\"nofollow external nofollow\" onclick=\"this.target='_blank';\" target=\"_blank\">Fritzing project page</a></p>\n<p>Connect three wires to the Arduino board. The first goes to ground from one of the outer pins of the potentiometer. The second goes from 5 volts to the other outer pin of the potentiometer. The third goes from analog input 0 to the middle pin of the potentiometer.</p>\n<p>For this example, it is possible to use the Arduino board’s built in LED attached to pin 13. To use an additional LED, attach its longer leg (the positive leg, or anode), to digital pin 13, and it’s shorter leg (the negative leg, or cathode) to the ground (gnd) pin next to pin 13. Because of the low amount of current coming from digital pin 13, it is not necessary to use a current limiting resistor in this particular case.</p>\n<h3>Schematic</h3>\n<p><a href=\"http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input-schematic.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-4040\" alt=\"Arduino Analog Input schematic\" src=\"http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input-schematic.jpg\" width=\"503\" height=\"610\" srcset=\"http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input-schematic.jpg 503w, http://duino4projects.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Arduino-Analog-Input-schematic-247x300.jpg 247w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 503px) 100vw, 503px\"></a></p>\n<h3>Code</h3>\n<p>In the beginning of this program, the variable&nbsp;<code>sensorPin</code>&nbsp;is set to to analog pin 0, where your potentiometer is attached, and&nbsp;<code>ledPin</code>&nbsp;is set to digital pin 13. You’ll also create another variable,&nbsp;<code>sensorValue</code>&nbsp;i to store the values read from your sensor.</p>\n<p>The&nbsp;<code>analogRead()</code>&nbsp;command converts the input voltage range, 0 to 5 volts, to a digital value between 0 and 1023. This is done by a circuit inside the Arduino called an&nbsp;<strong>analog-to-digital converter</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>ADC</strong>.</p>\n<p>By turning the shaft of the potentiometer, you change the amount of resistance on either side of the center pin (or wiper) of the potentiometer. This changes the relative resistances between the center pin and the two outside pins, giving you a different voltage at the analog input. When the shaft is turned all the way in one direction, there is no resistance between the center pin and the pin connected to ground.</p>\n<div class=\"box_ box right\" style=\"font-family:verdana;font-size:14 px; line-height:24px;-moz-border-radius: 20 px; border-radius: 20 px;background-color:#FFF8CB;color:#985D00;border-color:#985D12;\">\n<h3 class=\"box_head\" style=\"border-bottom-color:#985D12; background-color:#FFEB70;color:#985D00;-moz-border-radius-topleft:20 ; -moz-border-radius-topright:20 px; border-top-left-radius:20 px; border-top-right-radius:20 px;\">Major Components in Project</h3>\n<h3>Hardware Required</h3>\n<ul>\n<li>Arduino Board</li>\n<li>Potentiometer</li>\n<li>built-in LED on pin 13</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>For more detail:&nbsp;<a title=\"Analog Input using Arduino\" href=\"http://arduino.cc/en/Tutorial/AnalogInput\" rel=\"external nofollow\" onclick=\"this.target='_blank';\" target=\"_blank\">Analog Input using Arduino</a><!--Ad Injection:bottom--></p>\n<div style=\"padding-top:5px;\"><center><p></p>\n<p><span class=\"adedda\" style=\"font-family: lato; text-decoration: none ! important; font-size:
